Automobile News

Commentary

World Road Association Solves the Problem of Automobile Accidents 198

— Zhi

▲Promulgated Five Measures ▲Unanimously Accepted by All Countries

Vehicle congestion and automobile accidents are the most serious problems at present. All countries feel the seriousness, but in fact, it is still difficult to remedy. Now, this difficult problem has been substantially resolved. The organization that solved this difficult problem is the World Road Association, which held its meeting in Washington this May.

The World Road Association is dedicated to discussing facts and does not indulge in empty talk. At its first and second congresses, it drafted the automobile restriction law and immediately sent it to various countries for use. As a result, since 1926, twenty-three countries have implemented and adopted it. The number of other large cities that have done so is even more difficult to count. Therefore, in the first chapter of the opening statement, considerable respect must be paid to the World Road Association.

This year's congress has made even more progress. Its greatest achievement is the drafting and revision of three types of regulations. The first is a uniform automobile law (for government use), the second is a model municipal traffic law (for use by various cities), and the third is a unified book of traffic signals and other signs. These three books are naturally another great contribution to the world. On the opening day of the meeting, the U.S. Secretary of Commerce, who was also the chairman of the meeting, Mr. Raymond, delivered a speech. He said, "Regarding the problem of automobile transportation, the number of messages sent to the Department of Commerce every day is like snowflakes, and as serious as war bulletins. In terms of automobile accident statistics, in the United States alone, there were 12,500 cases in 1920, which increased to 22,000 cases in 1925, 28,000 cases in 1928, and as many as 31,000 cases in 1929. Let us analyze it further. In 1920, there were 136 fatalities per 1,000 vehicles. In 1925, there were only 110 vehicles, and in 1926, there were 107 vehicles. It can be seen that although the total number of accidents increased, the ratio decreased. However, after 1926, the situation changed again. Last year (1929), the ratio increased to 117 vehicles.

"The ratio is indeed high. However, the degree of increase is not drastic. We have adopted considerable methods. What are the methods? First. The most serious train accidents at railroad crossings. We use various methods, such as improving public education and strengthening publicity. Second. Children are the most easily hit because they are innocent and do not know the dangers. However, we promote safety education in schools. Outside the school gate, we stipulate that they must be picked up and dropped off by adults. In this way, in the past seven years, the rate of children being hit has increased by less than 25%. Third. We have established a statistical committee. Each province will unify the accidents. Submit them for classification and research to find ways to remedy them. Fourth. Most importantly, all cities can understand the seriousness of the vehicle situation. I am from Chicago. Take Chicago as an example. There have been significant results in rescuing vehicle accidents and solving vehicle congestion. In 1929, automobile accidents decreased by 2% compared to 1928. The situation in the other fourteen cities, including San Francisco, St. Louis, Milwaukee, etc., is better than before.

The above is the chairman's report on the situation in the United States. Let's look at the resolutions of the World Road Association. There are five main categories. First, the implementation of vehicle affairs laws and regulations. Second, the education law for road users. Third, vehicle accident statistics. Fourth, the construction and maintenance of vehicle laws. Fifth, road equipment laws, etc. Regarding the first resolution, this article can discuss. The remaining four items will be discussed later.

When it comes to implementing vehicle affairs laws and regulations, the conference believes that most accident problems have a considerable amount of clues. Take the crossing road accidents as an example. Most of them are caused by the lack of signal equipment at the crossings. Therefore, considerable attention has been paid to this point in unifying the automobile law. Looking at the automobile owner's accident, there are only a few reasons. The most important is violating the traffic law. This must be strictly dealt with by the police law. Secondly, ignoring the "left-hand driving law". It is clear that one should drive on the left, but in places where there is no one, they drive around without any consideration. Therefore, the law also stipulates that it is strictly prohibited.

The most important thing is the conclusion of the conference. It said, "To remedy the problem of vehicle accidents, it is not only necessary to rely on the vehicle affairs law. It is necessary to have the assistance of police officers. If it is found that it is not legal, it will be sanctioned without any favoritism. Secondly, it is necessary to get the sympathy of the court. Now a accident case. The court takes it very lightly. A few dollars fine and a few days in prison must be completed. How can this kind of understatement eliminate the carelessness of the car owner? Therefore, this point should be asked for the court's assistance. Third. There must be self-awareness of the people. Why do you say that? For example, the people themselves come out to organize a committee. It specializes in supervising the court's adjudication of the municipal government. If there is any discrepancy, it represents the public opinion and makes a formal request and suggestion. Only in this way can we cooperate and have hope."

It is said that the representatives of all countries gladly agreed to the above suggestions.

By-products of the Ford Factory 199

— Huang Yingdai

▲ No Waste in the Factory

Ford is a leading American automobile manufacturer. In recent years, its business has expanded daily, and its profits have increased significantly, showing great promise. However, the reason for Ford's development lies solely in its proper management and effective operation. In the Ford factory, whether it be the main factory or branch factories, there is no waste. Its management method is truly excellent. The income from by-products alone is particularly astonishing.

According to Ford factory statistics, comparing 1929 with 1928 in terms of by-products alone, 1929 saw an increase of $2,570,100 in revenue. The total by-product income for 1928 was $16,774,672, while for 1929 it was $19,344,373. This report was issued by the factory, so it is quite reliable. In these times of fierce commercial warfare, the success or failure of a business depends solely on proper management. The increase in by-product revenue at the Ford factory in recent years not only reduces all expenses but also lowers the value of its products. There is no waste in the factory that is discarded and not used. Utilizing waste is a win-win situation.

There is no waste in the Ford factory, as mentioned above. The sole purpose of various raw materials is to manufacture automobiles, which is known to all. However, in addition to manufacturing automobiles, countless by-products can be generated, either to be sold in the market or transported to branch factories for use. Last year, the revenue from the sale of by-products alone exceeded $19,000,000. In addition, the value of various by-products used by the Ford factory itself should also be in the millions of dollars. Last year, the most profitable by-product for sale was various scrap materials, with a total value of $5,672,000, an increase of $2,053,000 compared to the previous year.

Among the various by-products produced by the Ford factory last year, coal sales were valued at over $2,758,000. Ford has coal mining factories in Kentucky and West Virginia for its own use. In addition to its own use, coal is sold to others. Some is transported by rail to coal merchants across the central United States for sale, while some is shipped from the DeRouge Ford docks for use in branch factories in the Northwest. Within the coal mines, the Ford factory can also obtain by-products

Page 29

Coal tar. Last year, the total value was over $4,313,000. From the coal tar, 825,000 dollars' worth of ammonium chloride was extracted, which was actively promoted by Ford factory dealerships in various locations. This type of hydrochloric acid has become widely used recently. The light oil used when extracting coal tar can also yield hydrocarbons, which are used in the Detroit oil stations. Last year, sales of this product amounted to $2,357,000.

In the lumber mills that Ford established in northern Michigan, all wood chips and sawdust are distilled to obtain by-products such as charcoal and chemical products. Last year, the sales of charcoal alone amounted to $509,000, an increase of $147,000 compared to the previous year. Other materials such as rubber, cork, and artificial leather also saw an increase in revenue of $237,000 last year, with total sales of $561,000.

Iron slag and iron filings from the coal furnaces can be refined into Portland cement. Last year, sales of this amounted to $1,032,000. Other iron filings were purchased for road construction, totaling $169,000. The remaining gas was sold to a gas company in Detroit, generating $373,000 last year. Scraps of glass manufactured by the factory itself were sold for $579,000. The wood chips sold by the Michigan lumber mill amounted to $36,000. Johnson rules are produced in large quantities, with sales of $102,000 last year. These rules are made of metal and are widely used in countries around the world and are recognized by the U.S. Bureau of Standards as a standard measure. Ford initially intended to use them internally, but recently, they have been produced in excess, so they have been put up for sale. From the above, it can be seen that the annual by-product income of the Ford Motor Company is considerable.

The Development of Automobile and Road Industries in Soviet Russia 200

— Pei Gan

▲ 100,000 Automobiles Manufactured Annually

The total length of roads in Soviet Russia is currently three million kilometers, but only a small number of them are suitable for driving automobiles. According to statistics, it is no more than 50,000 kilometers. Therefore, the road conditions in various regions, cities, suburbs, and villages in Soviet Russia can be inferred from the above overview to get a general idea.

Given this situation, the roads in Soviet Russia must be reformed soon. It can be asserted that people in Soviet Russia now have a very common feeling that industrial center areas and densely populated areas must have suitable automobile roads. Currently, due to the lack of good roads in Soviet Russia, the total number of automobiles, including buses and trucks, is only over 21,000. Due to the lack of good roads, the automobile industry cannot develop. The scarcity of automobile production and the lack of emphasis on road issues are mutually causal. However, recently, there is a new organization in Soviet Russia called the Automobile Road Association, whose purpose is to realize the rapid advancement of both automobiles and roads.

This Automobile Road Association is exerting all its strength to awaken the people of Soviet Russia to pay attention to the construction of roads and the use of automobiles. The headquarters is located in Moscow, and there are branches everywhere. In terms of office work, the headquarters and branches are in contact with each other. The first goal of the association is to complete one million kilometers of paved roads and four and a half million kilometers of gravel roads within ten years. It is natural that this road construction will take place in densely populated areas, and its effectiveness can be anticipated.

In 1929, the Moscow Province designated 5,411,000 rubles to build major roads in the city of Moscow, and another 10,240,000 rubles were allocated for the construction of new roads throughout the province. Moscow began to have a public bus system in 1925, and today it has become an indispensable tool for public transportation and transport. At the end of 1928, there were 160 buses in Moscow, but this number was still in short supply. Moreover, due to narrow streets and crowded pedestrians, the buses found it very difficult to operate. According to the new plan for 1929, many new vehicles were added, and many roads were expanded. Currently, one and a half percent of the roads in Soviet Russia are gravel roads, a small number are paved stone roads, but the rest are mud roads with very simple construction.

Soviet Russia now plans to manufacture large numbers of automobiles to meet urgent needs. According to the plan of the Automobile Road Association, the annual automobile production must reach as many as 100,000 vehicles. If the needs of roads cannot advance in parallel with the needs of automobiles, then that is contrary to common sense. Therefore, in addition to good roads, the people of Soviet Russia are also gradually expanding the use of trucks and buses to facilitate transportation. Under these circumstances, in the next five years, Soviet Russia's attention to road construction will be even greater than in other countries around the world. Government officials know that the construction of good automobile roads is much cheaper than the construction of railways, and the benefits are also greater than those of railways. The road construction engineers have mostly returned from abroad, understand all kinds of benefits, and have sufficient experience. The Soviet government is very willing for foreign tourists to travel to its various regions and knows that good roads and automobile travel are the greatest assistance for this endeavor.

In the next few years, one thing that will occupy an important position in road development is the development of combined agricultural land. It is obvious that railway lines cannot reach large farms of 500,000 or 1,000,000 mu. Therefore, trucks for agricultural use will be used extensively. The economic and practical nature of automobile transportation and the promotion of state farms mean that good roads will solve all agricultural transportation needs. As for the progressive spirit of the leaders of the Automobile Road Association, their completion of the national road plan is even more certain.

Service as the Key to Commerce 201

— Ji Ren

▲ The Vanguard of Promoting Goods ▲ What the Automobile Industry Should Focus On

Business and trade, both buyers and sellers, all consider the deal done once the goods are exchanged, with no further responsibility. This has been the state of business for thousands of years. In recent years, with the development of industry and commerce and the intensification of competition, in order to expand business and attract customers, it is necessary to cater to the psychology of customers and obtain customer satisfaction. This is nothing other than service.

Even a few years ago, automobile transactions were the same. The manufacturer sold the vehicle to the buyer, and if the engine was free from defects and the driving was smooth, the responsibility was complete. The car owner, having obtained the car and feeling satisfied, had no other requests.

In recent years, the business situation has changed greatly, and business is becoming increasingly difficult. Car owners who purchase a car not only seek excellent engine performance at the time of purchase but also require a guarantee of long-term service in the future, so that the capital invested will yield full benefits. Therefore, manufacturers have no choice but to follow the psychology of car owners and establish branches, service stations, repair stations, and parts warehouses around the world to engage in service and expand business. Therefore, an additional expense is added, which is also very large.

The most perfect automobile service in the world today is the General Motors Corporation, the largest in the world. The scale is unparalleled. The factory now has branches in 114 countries, and there are service stations in various locations. Today, there are more than seven million General Motors cars on the road, which shows how prevalent they are. According to Mr. McDonald, the service director of the Shanghai branch of the factory in China, service is not only the responsibility of the car dealership but also an essential element in promoting vehicles. Car owners who receive perfect service are satisfied and spread the word, which is more effective than advertising. Promotion is more effective than talking.

Today, General Motors car owners, wherever they go, can carry their cars without worry. There is always a General Motors manager's service station nearby to provide repairs and service by specialists. The General Motors Corporation is deeply aware of the close relationship between service and business. It spares no expense to establish service stations for each car and has parts directors, service directors, and representatives who constantly communicate and discuss with managers and cooperate with each other. At the same time, it founded the General Motors Service School to train specialists to serve the Chinese people in the future. Its forward-thinking design and thorough service can be a model for the automobile industry.

1931 Chrysler Arrives in Shanghai 202

— Ke

▲ Mr. Odlum is Very Satisfied with its Use as a Means of Transportation

Mr. Robert Odlum, owner of the Dollar Steamship Company, arrived in Shanghai on the President Grant. On the same ship was the first batch of 1931 Chrysler eight-cylinder cars, which are currently on display in the showroom of the Mackie Motors Company at the corner of Szechuan Road and Edward Road.

After the car arrived in Shanghai, Mr. Mackie personally drove and invited Mr. Odlum to take a test drive. Mr. Odlum praised the new car highly, saying, "I have never seen a more beautiful car than this. I have never ridden in a more comfortable car than this."

This new Chrysler eight-cylinder car is one of the two major exports of the Chrysler factory this year, including features such as elegance, beauty, richness, engineering improvements, and increased speed.

In addition, there are various features not commonly seen on automobiles, which are all the crystallization of the time and skills of Chrysler's exclusive engineers. The Chrysler sedan currently on display in the showroom has a dark blue body, with unique fenders, a radiator that can be opened and closed, and all-metal spare tire racks.

A new Chrysler Royal eight-cylinder car will also arrive in Shanghai soon. The above two cars have reached the peak of engineering. All of Chrysler's famous acceleration, power, economy, driving convenience, comfort, and durability are further enhanced.

According to reliable sources, at Mr. Odlum's request, Mackie Motors has specially allocated a new car for Mr. Odlum's use as a means of transportation during his stay in Shanghai.

Talking About the Current Situation of Long-Distance Buses in Guangzhou 203

— Bi Ren

Since the active development of Guangzhou, transportation has become more convenient, and long-distance buses travel back and forth. However, the exact number of vehicles and their current situation are rarely known. Because the matter concerns the city's transportation, the author conducted a detailed investigation and recorded it in this column to inform readers.

Among the long-distance buses in Guangzhou that have been put into operation, in addition to city-operated vehicles and reserve vehicles from various companies, there are the Guomin, Limin, Fuli, Lihang, Tongxing, Mofan, Guangdong, Guangzhou, Baida, and Jiaotong companies, totaling 67 vehicles. Companies in the planning stage include the Zhonghua, Yangcheng, and Anmin companies, each with 10 vehicles, scheduled to run on the lines from Zhongshan Park to Lizhiwan, Sun Yat-sen University to Longjin Bridge, and Zhongshan Park to Daiheji. It is found that except for the Guangzhou, Mofan, and Tongxing companies, which can barely support themselves, the rest are in an unstable state. The reasons for the losses are roughly twofold. The gasoline and parts for the automobiles are all dependent on foreigners. Recently, the price of gold has skyrocketed, and the impact has been that the prices of all goods have risen. The price of gasoline has more than doubled compared to before. Moreover, the number of free-riding passengers is unparalleled elsewhere. Therefore, seats are often full, but there are few ticket sellers. Ticket revenue has also been greatly affected.

London to Hold Automobile Exhibition 206

— Ping Baoshan

London, England, will hold the world's largest automobile exhibition in the middle of next month. Products from seven other countries will be displayed inside to compete. British manufacturers are taking this action in the hope of expanding their overseas market and seeking smooth sales.

About 74 automobile manufacturing companies are participating in this unprecedented event, but the United Kingdom accounts for the largest number.

The United States has the second largest number of exhibits. France, Italy, Germany, Belgium, and Austria are next, and they will all inevitably lower their prices.

The cheapest car will be British, valued at 125 pounds, while the most expensive will be a German sample, reaching 3,000 pounds per vehicle.

The rest of the British products are priced lower than the same American vehicles. This is nothing more than advertising.

New Invention in Automobile Engineering 207

The diagram shows a new safety device called Sure Gard and how it communicates with the insurance stem, but as soon as the insurance stem is subjected to pressure, it can cut off the current. Two copper springs make contact, and the car stops abruptly. When the insurance stem touches an external object and the current stops, a spark in the electric ring causes this device to operate and automatically stall the engine.

This device can also be operated by installing an insurance button on the dashboard inside the car. If the driver anticipates danger ahead, pressing this button will stop the car much faster than using the foot brake or hand brake. At the same time, it does not conflict with the original brake. In crowded areas, where there is fear of accidentally colliding with the car in front and stopping, this device can be temporarily turned off. When parking, the current in the insurance stem can be connected to the horn to warn other drivers when needed.

Miscellaneous

Bad Driving Habits 208

— Ke Luo

When doing anything, it is important to lay a good foundation and develop good habits from the beginning, so that you can be spared a lot of trouble in the future.

Driving is related to the lives of oneself and others. Extra care should be taken. Driving a car seems very simple, but it is not easy to drive properly and legally. Constant practice is required. Developing good driving habits will prevent any danger and reduce many costs. There are many bad driving habits. Here are a few of the most common ones:

(2) Driving too fast. The engine operates too violently.

(1) Uneven acceleration. Randomly using the accelerator.

(3) If the star plug is clogged with dust, gasoline consumption increases by about 20%.

(4) Starting too abruptly. Rushing into intersections.

(5) Instant braking. Damages the brake system and is extremely dangerous.

(6) Using first or second gear for too long. The speed and action are weakened as a result.

Drivers often do not pay attention to things like this, which can damage the engine, hinder movement, cause danger, increase costs, and cause endless troubles. According to the advice of Mr. McDonald (service director of General Motors Corporation), any slight damage to the engine should be repaired immediately. This can save a lot of trouble. In addition, the engine should be inspected frequently to maintain the normal state of the parts and prevent accidents.
